Section 1:
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 SENATE BILL NO. 437
2 INTRODUCED BY C. GLIMM
3
4 A BILL FOR AN ACT ENTITLED: “AN ACT FOR THE CODIFICATION AND GENERAL REVISION OF THE
5 LAWS RELATING TO THE DEFINITION FOR THE WORDS SEX, FEMALE, AND MALE, MAN, WOMAN,
6 FATHER, AND MOTHER WHEN REFERRING TO A HUMAN; PROVIDING THAT THE DEFINITION OF SEX
7 REFERS TO BIOLOGICAL SEX AND NOT GENDER IDENTITY OR SEXUAL INTERCOURSE; PROVIDING
8 THAT THE DEFINITION OF SEX IS LIMITED TO TWO TYPES OF SEXES WHICH ARE REFERRED TO AS
9 MALE AND FEMALE; PROVIDING THAT THE DEFINITIONS OF MALE, AND FEMALE, MAN, WOMAN,
10 FATHER, AND MOTHER REFER TO BIOLOGICAL SEX AND NOT SUBJECTIVE GENDER IDENTITY;
11 CLARIFYING THE MEANING OF THE TERM "GENDER"; PROVIDING FOR EXCEPTIONS; AMENDING
12 SECTIONS 2-18-208, 2-18-606, 7-15-4207, 7-34-2123, 10-2-403, 13-27-408, 13-35-301, 13-38-201, 13-38-
13 203, 13-38-205, 19-2-802, 20-6-808, 20-7-1306, 20-7-1703, 20-9-327, 20-11-116, 20-25-501, 20-25-707, 22-2-
14 306, 23-2-505, 33-1-201, 35-20-209, 39-2-912, 39-29-101, 39-71-401, 40-1-107, 40-1-311, 40-1-401, 40-5-804,
15 40-5-907, 40-5-1031, 40-6-701, 40-6-703, 41-3-210, 41-5-103, 42-2-204, 44-2-411, 44-2-412, 45-5-625, 46-18-
16 101, 46-19-301, 46-19-401, 49-1-102, 49-2-101, 49-3-101, 50-4-720, 50-5-105, 50-5-602, 50-11-101, 50-15-
17 101, 50-19-103, 50-19-501, 50-60-214, 53-20-142, 53-21-121, 53-21-142, 53-24-310, 53-30-312, 60-5-514, 60-
18 5-522, 61-5-107, 72-1-103, 72-17-106, AND 90-14-104, MCA; REPEALING SECTION 1-1-201, MCA; AND
19 PROVIDING AN IMMEDIATE EFFECTIVE DATE.”
20
21 WHEREAS, IN HUMAN BEINGS, THERE ARE TWO -- AND ONLY TWO -- SEXES: MALE AND FEMALE, WHICH REFER
22 TO THE TWO BODY STRUCTURES (PHENOTYPES) THAT, IN NORMAL DEVELOPMENT, CORRESPOND TO ONE OR THE OTHER
23 GAMETE -- SPERM FOR MALES AND OVA FOR FEMALES; AND
24 WHEREAS, EVERY INDIVIDUAL IS EITHER MALE OR FEMALE; AND
25 WHEREAS, AN INDIVIDUAL'S SEX CAN BE OBSERVED OR CLINICALLY VERIFIED AT OR BEFORE BIRTH; AND
26 WHEREAS, RARE DISORDERS OF SEXUAL DEVELOPMENT ARE NOT EXCEPTIONS TO THE BINARY NATURE OF
27 SEX; AND
28 WHEREAS, IN NO CASE IS AN INDIVIDUAL'S SEX DETERMINED BY STIPULATION OR SELF-IDENTIFICATION; AND
- 1 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 WHEREAS, THERE IS INCREASING CONFUSION ABOUT THE DEFINITION AND IMPLICATIONS OF SEX AS A
2 BIOLOGICAL TRUTH AND ITS RELATIONSHIP TO CONCEPTS AND TERMS INCLUDING BUT NOT LIMITED TO SEX ASSIGNED AT
3 BIRTH, GENDER, GENDER IDENTITY, GENDER ROLE, GENDER EXPRESSION, AND EXPERIENCED GENDER; AND
4 WHEREAS, CONFUSION AND AMBIGUITIES SURROUNDING THE DEFINITIONS OF SEX, MALE, FEMALE, AND
5 RELATED TERMS CAN HINDER INDIVIDUAL EFFORTS TO ENJOY EQUAL TREATMENT UNDER THE LAW; AND
6 WHEREAS, LEGAL EQUALITY OF THE TWO SEXES -- MALE AND FEMALE -- DOES NOT IMPLY THAT THE SEXES
7 ARE IDENTICAL TO EACH OTHER OR ARE THE SAME IN EVERY RESPECT; AND
8 WHEREAS, WITH RESPECT TO THE TWO SEXES -- MALE AND FEMALE -- SEPARATE FACILITIES OR SPORTS
9 LEAGUES ESTABLISHED BECAUSE OF OR ORGANIZED ACCORDING TO PHYSICAL DIFFERENCES BETWEEN THE SEXES DO
10 NOT CONSTITUTE UNEQUAL TREATMENT UNDER THE LAW; AND
11 WHEREAS, PHYSICAL DIFFERENCES BETWEEN MALES AND FEMALES ARE ENDURING, AND THE TWO SEXES ARE
12 NOT FUNGIBLE.
13 THEREFORE, IT IS THE INTENT OF THE LEGISLATURE OF THIS STATE TO CLARIFY AND RECONCILE THE
14 MEANING OF SEX, MALE, FEMALE, AND RELATED TERMS IN STATE LAWS, ADMINISTRATIVE RULES, AND GUIDELINES.
15
16 BE IT ENACTED BY THE LEGISLATURE OF THE STATE OF MONTANA:
17
18 NEW SECTION. Section 1. Terms of wide applicability. (1) Unless the context requires otherwise,
19 the following definitions apply in the Montana Code Annotated:
20 (a) "FATHER" MEANS A MALE PARENT.
21 (B) "Female" means a member of the human species who, under normal development, has XX
22 chromosomes and produces or would produce relatively large, relatively immobile gametes, or eggs, during her
23 life cycle and has a reproductive and endocrine system oriented around the production of those gametes. An
24 individual who would otherwise fall within this definition, but for a biological or genetic condition, is female, WHEN
25 USED TO REFER TO A NATURAL PERSON, AN INDIVIDUAL WHO NATURALLY HAS, HAD, WILL HAVE, OR WOULD HAVE, BUT
26 FOR A CONGENITAL ANOMALY OR INTENTIONAL OR UNINTENTIONAL DISRUPTION, THE REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEM THAT AT
27 SOME POINT PRODUCES, TRANSPORTS, AND UTILIZES THE LARGE GAMETE, OR OVA, FOR FERTILIZATION.
28 (b)(C) "Male" means a member of the human species who, under normal development, has XY
- 2 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 chromosomes and produces or would produce small, mobile gametes, or sperm, during his life cycle and has a
2 reproductive and endocrine system oriented around the production of those gametes. An individual who would
3 otherwise fall within this definition, but for a biological or genetic condition, is male, WHEN USED TO REFER TO A
4 NATURAL PERSON, AN INDIVIDUAL WHO NATURALLY HAS, HAD, WILL HAVE, OR WOULD HAVE, BUT FOR A CONGENITAL
5 ANOMALY OR INTENTIONAL OR UNINTENTIONAL DISRUPTION, THE REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEM THAT AT SOME POINT
6 PRODUCES, TRANSPORTS, AND UTILIZES THE SMALL GAMETE, OR SPERM, FOR FERTILIZATION.
7 (c)(D) "MAN" MEANS AN ADULT HUMAN MALE, EXCEPT WHEN USED AS A GENERIC REFERENCE TO HUMAN
8 BEINGS.
9 (E) "MOTHER" MEANS A FEMALE PARENT.
10 (F) "Oath" includes an affirmation or declaration.
11 (d)(G) "Person" includes a corporation or other entity as well as a natural person.
12 (e)(H) "Several" means two or more.
13 (f)(I) "Sex" means the organization of the body parts and gametes for reproduction in human beings
14 and other organisms. In human beings, there are exactly two sexes, male and female, with two corresponding
15 types of gametes. The sexes are determined by the biological and genetic indication of male or female,
16 including sex chromosomes, naturally occurring sex chromosomes, gonads, and nonambiguous internal and
17 external genitalia present at birth, without regard to an individual's psychological, behavioral, social, chosen, or
18 subjective experience of gender WHETHER SOMEONE IS MALE OR FEMALE, WHICH IS DISTINGUISHED BASED ON THE
19 TYPE OF GAMETE, SPERM OR EGGS, THEY ARE CAPABLE OF OR EXPECTED TO PRODUCE, AS DICTATED BY THEIR PRIMARY
20 SEXUAL ANATOMY. BECAUSE THERE ARE ONLY TWO TYPES OF GAMETES, SPERM AND OVA, WITH TWO CORRESPONDING
21 REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEMS, THERE ARE ONLY TWO SEXES: MALE AND FEMALE. AN INDIVIDUAL'S SEX IS ROOTED IN
22 REPRODUCTIVE ANATOMY AND IS IN NO WAY INFLUENCED OR DEFINED BY ONE'S PSYCHOLOGICAL STATE, BEHAVIOR,
23 EXPRESSION, OR PERSONAL IDENTITY.
24 (g)(J) "State", when applied to the different parts of the United States, includes the District of
25 Columbia and the territories.
26 (h)(K) "United States" includes the District of Columbia and the territories.
27 (L) "WOMAN" MEANS AN ADULT HUMAN FEMALE.
28 (2) Wherever the word "man" or "men" or a word that includes the syllable "man" or "men" in
- 3 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 combination with other syllables, such as "workman", appears in this code, the word or syllable includes
2 "woman" or "women" unless the context clearly indicates a contrary intent and unless the subject matter of the
3 statute relates clearly and necessarily to a specific sex only.
4 (3) Whenever the term "heretofore" occurs in any statute, it must be construed to mean any time
5 previous to the day the statute takes effect. Whenever the word "hereafter" occurs, it must be construed to
6 mean the time after the statute containing the term takes effect.
7 (4) (A) THE TERM "GENDER", WHEN USED ALONE TO REFER TO A MALE, FEMALE, OR THE NATURAL
8 DIFFERENCES BETWEEN A MALE AND FEMALE:
9 (I) MUST BE CONSIDERED A SYNONYM FOR SEX; AND
10 (II) MAY NOT BE CONSIDERED A SYNONYM OR SHORT-HAND EXPRESSION FOR GENDER IDENTITY,
11 EXPERIENCED GENDER, GENDER EXPRESSION, OR GENDER ROLE.
12 (B) THE TERM "GENDER" DOES NOT APPLY WHEN IT IS USED IN CONJUNCTION WITH OTHER WORDS OR AS
13 AN ADJECTIVE TO MODIFY OTHER WORDS, OR WHEN CONTEXT OR EXPLICIT DEFINITION IN PREEXISTING STATE LAW,
14 ADMINISTRATIVE RULES, OR GUIDELINES INDICATES OTHERWISE.
15 (C) THE TERM "GENDER IDENTITY", IF USED IN STATE LAW, ADMINISTRATIVE RULES, OR GUIDELINES, MAY
16 NOT BE CONSIDERED A SYNONYM OR SUBSTITUTE FOR SEX OR GENDER.
17
18 Section 2. Section 2-18-208, MCA, is amended to read:
19 "2-18-208. Comparable worth. The department of administration shall, in its continuous efforts to
20 enhance the current classification plan and pay schedules, work toward the goal of establishing a standard of
21 equal pay for comparable worth. This standard for the classification plan shall be reached by:
22 (1) eliminating, in the classification of positions, the use of judgments and factors that contain
23 inherent biases based on sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1]; and
24 (2) comparing, in the classification of positions, the factors for determining job worth across
25 occupational groups whenever those groups are dominated by males or females."
26
27 SECTION 3. SECTION 2-18-606, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:
28 "2-18-606. Parental leave for state employees. (1) The department of administration shall develop a

10 Section 4. Section 7-15-4207, MCA, is amended to read:
11 "7-15-4207. Prohibition against discrimination. For all of the purposes of this part and part 43, a
12 person may not be subjected to discrimination because of sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], race, creed,
13 religion, age, physical or mental disability, color, or national origin."

15 Section 5. Section 7-34-2123, MCA, is amended to read:
16 "7-34-2123. Admission to district hospital facilities. Such a hospital district must admit persons to
17 its facilities without regard to race, color, or sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1]. Such obligation shall not
18 prevent the board of trustees of such hospital district from establishing reasonable minimum rates for hospital
19 quarters, services, and supplies. Indigents needing such services, for the rendition of which provision is made
20 by the laws of Montana, must be admitted to such public hospitals on terms and rates prescribed or authorized
21 by law."

8 Section 7. Section 13-27-408, MCA, is amended to read:
9 "13-27-408. Rejection of improper arguments. The secretary of state shall reject, with the approval
10 of the attorney general, an argument or other matter held to contain obscene, vulgar, profane, scandalous,
11 libelous, or defamatory matter; any language that in any way incites, counsels, promotes, or advocates hatred,
12 abuse, violence, or hostility toward, or that tends to cast ridicule or shame upon, a group of persons by reason
13 of race, color, religion, or sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], sexual orientation, sexual identity, or sexual
14 expression; or any matter not allowed to be sent through the mail. Such arguments may not be filed or printed
15 in the voter information pamphlet."

17 Section 8. Section 13-35-301, MCA, is amended to read:
18 "13-35-301. Adoption of code of fair campaign practices. The following code of fair campaign
19 practices is adopted by Montana:
20 "There are basic principles of decency, honesty, and fair play that every candidate for public office in
21 the United States has a moral obligation to observe and uphold, in order that, after vigorously contested but
22 fairly conducted campaigns, our citizens may exercise their constitutional right to a free and untrammeled
23 choice and the will of the people may be fully and clearly expressed on the issues before the country.
24 Therefore:
25 I will conduct my campaign in the best American tradition, discussing the issues as I see them,
26 presenting my record and policies with sincerity and frankness, and criticizing without fear or favor the record
27 and policies of my opponent and my opponent's party that merit such criticism.
28 I will defend and uphold the right of every qualified American voter to full and equal participation in the
- 6 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 electoral process.
2 I will conduct my campaign without the use of personal vilification, character defamation, whispering
3 campaigns, libel, slander, or scurrilous attacks on my opposition or my opposition's personal or family life.
4 I will not use campaign material of any sort that misrepresents, distorts, or otherwise falsifies the facts,
5 nor will I use malicious or unfounded accusations that aim at creating or exploiting doubts, without justification,
6 as to the loyalty and patriotism of my opposition.
7 I will not make any appeal to prejudice based on race, sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], creed, or
8 national origin.
9 I will not undertake or condone any dishonest or unethical practice that tends to corrupt or undermine
10 our American system of free elections or that hampers or prevents the full and free expression of the will of the
11 voters.
12 Insofar as is possible, I will immediately and publicly repudiate support deriving from any individual or
13 group that resorts, on behalf of my candidacy or in opposition to that of my opponent, to the methods and
14 tactics that I have pledged not to use or condone.""

16 Section 9. Section 13-38-201, MCA, is amended to read:
17 "13-38-201. Election or appointment of committee representatives at primary -- vacancies -- tie
18 votes. (1) Each political party shall appoint or elect at each primary election one person of each sex, as defined
19 in 1-1-201 [section 1], to serve as committee representatives for each election precinct. The committee
20 representatives must be residents and registered voters of the precinct.
21 (2) If a political party chooses to appoint precinct committee representatives, the political party
22 shall make the appointments as provided in the party's rules.

24 (a) administer the election itself as provided in the party's rules; or
25 (b) elect precinct committee representatives in a primary election, subject to 13-10-209 and
26 subsection (4) of this section.
27 (4) In a primary election for a precinct committee representative:
28 (a) if the number of candidates nominated for a party's precinct committee representatives is less

26 10-327 must be open to the public. Records of a central committee regarding filling a vacancy pursuant to 13-

3 SECTION 11. SECTION 13-38-205, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:
4 "13-38-205. Organization and operation of county and city central committees. (1) The county
5 central committee shall meet prior to the state convention of its political party and organize by electing a
6 presiding officer and one or more vice presiding officers. The gender, as provided in [section 1], of the presiding
7 officer and the vice presiding officer may not be the same. The county central committee shall elect a secretary
8 and other officers as necessary. It is not necessary for the officers to be precinct committee representatives.
9 (2) The committee may select managing or executive committees and authorize subcommittees to
10 exercise all powers conferred upon the county, city, state, and congressional central committees by the election
11 laws of this state.
12 (3) The presiding officer of the county central committee shall call the county convention and not
13 less than 4 days before the date of the county convention shall publish the call in a newspaper published at the
14 county seat and mail a copy of the call to each precinct committee representative. If party rules permit the use
15 of a proxy, a proxy may not be recognized unless it is held by an elector of the precinct of the committee
16 representative executing it.
17 (4) The county presiding officer of the party shall preside at the county convention. No person
18 other than a duly elected or appointed committee representative or officer of the committee is entitled to
19 participate in the proceedings of the committee.
20 (5) If a committee representative is absent, the convention may fill the vacancy by appointing some
21 qualified elector of the party, resident in the precinct, to represent the precinct in the convention.
22 (6) The county convention shall elect delegates and alternate delegates to the state convention
23 under rules of the state party. The presiding officer and secretary of the county convention shall issue and sign
24 certificates of election of the delegates."
25
26 SECTION 12. SECTION 19-2-802, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:

24 state.
25 (b) A school district may not require a student enrolled in the school district to attend a public
26 charter school.
27 (c) A public charter school may limit admission to students within a given age group or grade level.
28 (d) A public charter school may be organized for a special emphasis, theme, or concept as stated

2 (e) A public charter school shall enroll all students who wish to attend the school unless the
3 number of students exceeds the capacity of a program, class, grade level, or building.
4 (f) If capacity is insufficient to enroll all students who wish to attend the school, the public charter
5 school shall select students through a lottery.

8 (b) A public charter school may give enrollment preference to:

20 school in this state, the student's new school shall accept credits earned by the student in courses or
21 instructional programs at the public charter school.

23 public charter schools as an enrollment option within the district to the same extent and through the same
24 means that the district provides and publicizes information about noncharter public schools in the district.
25 (6) The board of public education may not restrict the number of students a public charter school
26 may enroll. The capacity of the public charter school must be determined annually by the governing board in
27 consideration of the public charter school's ability to facilitate the academic success of its students, to achieve
28 the objectives specified in the charter contract, and to ensure that its student enrollment does not exceed the

3 Section 14. Section 20-7-1306, MCA, is amended to read:
4 "20-7-1306. (Temporary) Designation of athletic teams. (1) Interscholastic, intercollegiate,
5 intramural, or club athletic teams or sports that are sponsored by a public elementary or high school, a public
6 institution of higher education, or any school or institution whose students or teams compete against a public
7 school or institution of higher education must be expressly designated as one of the following based on
8 biological sex:
9 (a) males, men, or boys;
10 (b) females, women, or girls; or
11 (c) coed or mixed.
12 (2) Athletic teams or sports designated for females, women, or girls may not be open to students of
13 the male sex.
14 (3) For the purposes of this section, "female", "male", and "sex" are defined in 1-1-201 [section 1].
15 (Void on occurrence of contingency--sec. 6, Ch. 405, L. 2021.)"

17 Section 15. Section 20-7-1703, MCA, is amended to read:
18 "20-7-1703. Definitions. As used in this part, the following definitions apply:
19 (1) "Eligible postsecondary institution" means an accredited postsecondary institution located in
20 Montana.

10 SECTION 17. SECTION 20-11-116, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:
11 "20-11-116. Enrollment. (1) (a) A community choice school must be open to any student residing in
12 the state.
13 (b) A school district may not require a student enrolled in the school district to attend a choice
14 school.
15 (c) A choice school may limit admission to students within a given age group or grade level.
16 (d) A choice school may be organized for a special emphasis, theme, or concept as stated in the
17 school's proposal.
18 (e) A choice school shall enroll all students who wish to attend the school unless the number of
19 students exceeds the capacity of a program, class, grade level, or building.
20 (f) If capacity is insufficient to enroll all students who wish to attend the school, the choice school
21 shall select students through a lottery.
22 (2) A traditional public school converting to a choice school shall adopt and maintain a policy
23 giving enrollment preference to students who reside within the former attendance area of that public school.
24 (3) (a) A choice school shall give enrollment preference to students who were enrolled in the
25 choice school the previous school year and to siblings of students already enrolled in the choice school. An
26 enrollment preference for returning students and siblings excludes those students from entering a lottery.
27 (b) A choice school may give enrollment preference to children of a choice school's employees
28 and governing board, limited to no more than 10% of the school's total student population.
- 15 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 (4) This section does not preclude the formation of a community choice school for the purpose of
2 serving students with disabilities, students of the same gender, as provided in [section 1], students who pose a
3 sufficiently severe disciplinary problem to warrant a specific educational program, or students who are at risk of
4 academic failure. If capacity is insufficient to enroll all students who wish to attend a school, the choice school
5 shall select students through a lottery.
6 (5) If a student who was previously enrolled in a choice school enrolls in any other public school in
7 this state, the student's new school shall accept credits earned by the student in courses or instructional
8 programs at the choice school.
9 (6) A traditional school district shall provide or publicize to parents and the general public
10 information about choice schools as an enrollment option within the district's physical, geographical boundaries
11 to the same extent and through the same means that the district provides and publicizes information about
12 traditional public schools in the district.
13 (7) An authorizer may not restrict the number of students a choice school may enroll. The capacity
14 of the choice school must be determined annually by its governing board in conjunction with the authorizer and
15 in consideration of the choice school's ability to facilitate the academic success of its students, to achieve the
16 objectives specified in the charter contract, and to ensure that its student enrollment does not exceed the
17 capacity of its facility or site.
18 (8) If the choice school is the only public school in a town, the choice school must give preference
19 to enrolling pupils residing in the town or within 5 miles of the school if the next closest public school is more
20 than 10 miles away from the student's residence."

12 SECTION 21. SECTION 23-2-505, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:
13 "23-2-505. Owner's civil liability. The owner of a vessel is liable for any injury or damage
14 occasioned by the negligent operation of the vessel, whether the negligence consists of a violation of the
15 provisions of the statutes of this state or neglecting to observe ordinary care and operation that the rules of the
16 common law require. However, the owner is not liable unless the vessel is being used with the owner's express
17 or implied consent. It must be presumed that the vessel is being operated with the knowledge and consent of
18 the owner if, at the time of the injury or damage, it is under the control of the owner's spouse, father as defined
19 in [section 1], mother as defined in [section 1], brother, sister, son, daughter, or other immediate member of the
20 owner's family. This section may not be construed to relieve any other person from any liability that the person
21 would otherwise have. However, this section may not be construed to authorize or permit any recovery in
22 excess of injury or damage actually incurred."

1 "40-1-311. Declaration of marriage without solemnization. (1) Persons may consummate a
2 marriage by written declaration in this state without the solemnization provided for in 40-1-301. The declaration
3 must be filed by the clerk of the district court in the county where the contract was executed.
4 (2) A declaration of marriage must contain substantially the following:
5 (a) the names, ages, and residences of the parties;
6 (b) the fact of marriage;

10 (3) The declaration must be subscribed by the parties and attested by at least two witnesses and
11 formally acknowledged before the clerk of the district court of the county.
12 (4) The fee for filing a declaration is $53 and must be paid to the clerk at time of filing."

14 Section 29. Section 40-1-401, MCA, is amended to read:
15 "40-1-401. Prohibited marriages -- contracts. (1) The following marriages are prohibited:
16 (a) a marriage entered into prior to the dissolution of an earlier marriage of one of the parties;
17 (b) a marriage between an ancestor and a descendant or between a brother and a sister, whether
18 the relationship is by the half or the whole blood, or between first cousins;
19 (c) a marriage between an uncle and a niece or between an aunt and a nephew, whether the
20 relationship is by the half or the whole blood;
21 (d) a marriage between persons of the same sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1].
22 (2) Parties to a marriage prohibited under this section who cohabit after removal of the impediment
23 are lawfully married as of the date of the removal of the impediment.
24 (3) Children born of a prohibited marriage are legitimate.
25 (4) A contractual relationship entered into for the purpose of achieving a civil relationship that is
26 prohibited under subsection (1) is void as against public policy."

1 "40-5-804. Definitions. For purposes of this part, the following definitions apply:
2 (1) "Child" means an individual, whether over or under 18 years of age, to whom or on whose
3 behalf a legal duty of support is owed by a parent. The term includes but is not limited to a child enrolled or
4 eligible for enrollment under a health benefit plan or individual insurance policy.
5 (2) "Child support guidelines" means guidelines adopted under the provisions of 40-5-209.
6 (3) "COBRA" means the federal Consolidated Omnibus Budget Reconciliation Act of 1985, under
7 which dependent children of employees may continue to receive, for a limited time under specific
8 circumstances, health plan coverage after termination of employment.
9 (4) "Department" means the department of public health and human services as provided for in 2-
10 15-2201.
11 (5) (a) "Health benefit plan" or "plan" means a group health benefit plan or combination of plans
12 that provides medical care or benefits for a child. The term includes but is not limited to a health maintenance
13 organization, self-funded group, state or local government group health plan, church group plan, medical or
14 health service corporation, or similar plan.
15 (b) The term does not include public health coverage if other medical insurance is available to one
16 or both of the parents at a reasonable cost and is accessible for the child.
17 (6) "Individual insurance" means health or medical insurance coverage other than a group health
18 benefit plan or public assistance that is or may be provided individually for a child.
19 (7) "Medical care" means diagnosis, cure, mitigation, treatment, or prevention of disease, illness,
20 or injury, including well baby checkups, periodic examinations, and any other undertaking for the purpose of
21 affecting any structure or function of the body.
22 (8) "Medical support order" means a judgment, decree, or order, including approval of a settlement
23 agreement issued by a tribunal of competent jurisdiction, that provides for the medical care of a child and that
24 complies with the requirements of this part.
25 (9) "Obligated parent" means the parent who is required by a medical support order to provide for
26 the medical care of a child. The obligated parent is not necessarily the same as an obligor for child support.
27 (10) "Parent" means a father or mother, as defined in [section 1], and includes a child's guardian or
28 other adult caretaker having lawful charge of the child.

14 Section 33. Section 40-6-701, MCA, is amended to read:
15 "40-6-701. Interference with fundamental parental rights restricted -- cause of action. (1) A
16 government entity may not interfere with the fundamental right of parents to direct the upbringing, education,
17 health care, and mental health of their children unless the government entity demonstrates that the
18 interference:
19 (a) furthers a compelling governmental interest; and
20 (b) is narrowly tailored and is the least restrictive means available for the furthering of the
21 compelling governmental interest.
22 (2) All fundamental parental rights are exclusively reserved to the parent of a child without
23 obstruction or interference by a government entity, including but not limited to the rights and responsibilities to
24 do the following:
25 (a) direct the education of the child, including the right to choose public, private, religious, or home
26 schools and the right to make reasonable choices with public schools for the education of the child;
27 (b) access and review all written and electronic education records relating to the child that are
28 controlled by or in the possession of a school;

5 (g) consent before a biometric scan of the child is made, shared, or stored;
6 (h) consent before a record of the child's blood or DNA is created, stored, or shared, unless

10 corrections.
11 (b) If the offender is released after the mandatory minimum period of imprisonment, the offender is
12 subject to supervision by the department of corrections for the remainder of the offender's life and shall
13 participate in the program for continuous, satellite-based monitoring provided for in 46-23-1010.
14 (5) As used in this section, the following definitions apply:
15 (a) "Electronic communication" means a sign, signal, writing, image, sound, data, or intelligence of
16 any nature transmitted or created in whole or in part by a wire, radio, electromagnetic, photoelectronic, or
17 photo-optical system.
18 (b) "Sexual conduct" means:
19 (i) actual or simulated:
20 (A) sexual intercourse, whether between persons of the same or opposite sex, as defined in 1-1-
21 201 [section 1];
22 (B) penetration of the vagina or rectum by any object, except when done as part of a recognized
23 medical procedure;
24 (C) bestiality;
25 (D) masturbation;
26 (E) sadomasochistic abuse;
27 (F) lewd exhibition of the genitals, breasts, pubic or rectal area, or other intimate parts of any
28 person; or
- 52 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 (G) defecation or urination for the purpose of the sexual stimulation of the viewer; or
2 (ii) depiction of a child in the nude or in a state of partial undress with the purpose to abuse,
3 humiliate, harass, or degrade the child or to arouse or gratify the person's own sexual response or desire or the
4 sexual response or desire of any person.
5 (c) "Simulated" means any depicting of the genitals or pubic or rectal area that gives the
6 appearance of sexual conduct or incipient sexual conduct.
7 (d) "Visual medium" means:
8 (i) any film, photograph, videotape, negative, slide, or photographic reproduction that contains or
9 incorporates in any manner any film, photograph, videotape, negative, or slide; or
10 (ii) any disk, diskette, or other physical media that allows an image to be displayed on a computer
11 or other video screen and any image transmitted to a computer or other video screen by telephone line, cable,
12 satellite transmission, or other method."

14 SECTION 41. SECTION 46-18-101, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:
15 "46-18-101. Correctional and sentencing policy. (1) It is the purpose of this section to establish the
16 correctional and sentencing policy of the state of Montana. Laws for the punishment of crime are drawn to
17 implement the policy established by this section.
18 (2) The correctional and sentencing policy of the state of Montana is to:
19 (a) punish each offender commensurate with the nature and degree of harm caused by the offense
20 and to hold an offender accountable;
21 (b) protect the public, reduce crime, and increase the public sense of safety by incarcerating
22 violent offenders and serious repeat offenders;
23 (c) provide restitution, reparation, and restoration to the victim of the offense; and
24 (d) encourage and provide opportunities for the offender's self-improvement to provide
25 rehabilitation and reintegration of offenders back into the community.
26 (3) To achieve the policy outlined in subsection (2), the state of Montana adopts the following
27 principles:
28 (a) Sentencing and punishment must be certain, timely, consistent, and understandable.
- 53 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 (b) Sentences should be commensurate with the punishment imposed on other persons
2 committing the same offenses.
3 (c) Sentencing practices must be neutral with respect to the offender's race, gender, as provided in
4 [section 1], religion, national origin, or social or economic status.
5 (d) Sentencing practices must permit judicial discretion to consider aggravating and mitigating
6 circumstances.
7 (e) Sentencing practices must include punishing violent and serious repeat felony offenders with
8 incarceration.
9 (f) Sentencing practices must provide alternatives to imprisonment for the punishment of those
10 nonviolent felony offenders who do not have serious criminal records.
11 (g) Sentencing and correctional practices must emphasize that the offender is responsible for
12 obeying the law and must hold the offender accountable for the offender's actions.
13 (h) Sentencing practices must emphasize restitution to the victim by the offender. A sentence must
14 require an offender who is financially able to do so to pay restitution, costs as provided in 46-18-232, costs of
15 assigned counsel, as provided in 46-8-113, and, if the offender is a sex offender, costs of any chemical
16 treatment.
17 (i) Sentencing practices should promote and support practices, policies, and programs that focus
18 on restorative justice principles."

24 WESTERN INTERSTATE CORRECTIONS COMPACT
25 ARTICLE I
26 PURPOSE AND POLICY
27 The party states, desiring by common action to improve their institutional facilities and provide
28 programs of sufficiently high quality for the confinement, treatment, and rehabilitation of various types of
- 54 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

1 offenders, declare that it is the policy of each of the party states to provide such facilities and programs on the
2 basis of cooperation with one another, thereby serving the best interests of such offenders and of society. The
3 purpose of this compact is to provide for the development and execution of such programs of cooperation for
4 the confinement, treatment, and rehabilitation of offenders.
5 ARTICLE II
6 DEFINITIONS
7 As used in this compact, unless the context clearly requires otherwise:
8 (1) "state" means a state of the United States or, subject to the limitation contained in Article VII,
9 Guam;
10 (2) "sending state" means a state party to this compact in which conviction was had;
11 (3) "receiving state" means a state party to this compact to which an inmate is sent for confinement
12 other than a state in which conviction was had;
13 (4) "inmate" means a male or female, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], offender who is under
14 sentence to or confined in a prison or other correctional institution;
15 (5) "institution" means any prison, reformatory, or other correctional facility (including but not
16 limited to a facility for the mentally ill or mentally defective) in which inmates may lawfully be confined.

18 CONTRACTS
19 (1) Each party state may make one or more contracts with any one or more of the other party
20 states for the confinement of inmates on behalf of a sending state in institutions situated within receiving states.
21 Any such contract shall provide for:
22 (a) its duration;
23 (b) payments to be made to the receiving state by the sending state for inmate maintenance,
24 extraordinary medical and dental expenses, and any participation in or receipt by inmates of rehabilitative or
25 correctional services, facilities, programs, or treatment not reasonably included as part of normal maintenance;
26 (c) participation in programs of inmate employment, if any; the disposition or crediting of any

5 party state, any other party state or states may contract therewith for the enlargement of the planned capacity
6 of the institution or addition thereto, or for the inclusion therein of particular equipment or structures, and for the
7 reservation of a specific percent of the capacity of the institution to be kept available for use by inmates of the
8 sending state or states so contracting. Any sending state so contracting may, to the extent that moneys are
9 legally available therefor, pay to the receiving state a reasonable sum as consideration for such enlargement of

3 ARTICLE VII
4 ENTRY INTO FORCE
5 This compact shall enter into force and become effective and binding upon the states so acting when it
6 has been enacted into law by any two contiguous states from among the states of Alaska, Arizona, California,
7 Colorado, Hawaii, Idaho, Montana, Nebraska, Nevada, New Mexico, Oregon, Utah, Washington, and Wyoming.
8 For the purposes of this article, Alaska and Hawaii shall be deemed contiguous to each other; to any and all of
9 the states of California, Oregon, and Washington; and to Guam. Thereafter, this compact shall enter into force
10 and become effective and binding as to any other of said states or any other state contiguous to at least one
11 party state upon similar action by such state. Guam may become party to this compact by taking action similar
12 to that provided for joinder by any other eligible party state and upon the consent of congress to such joinder.
13 For the purposes of this article, Guam shall be deemed contiguous to Alaska, Hawaii, California, Oregon, and
14 Washington.
15 ARTICLE VIII
16 WITHDRAWAL AND TERMINATION
17 This compact shall continue in force and remain binding upon a party state until it shall have enacted a
18 statute repealing the same and providing for the sending of formal written notice of withdrawal from the
19 compact to the appropriate officials of all other party states. An actual withdrawal shall not take effect until 2
20 years after the notices provided in said statute have been sent. Such withdrawal shall not relieve the
21 withdrawing state from its obligations assumed hereunder prior to the effective date of withdrawal. Before the
22 effective date of withdrawal, a withdrawing state shall remove to its territory, at its own expense, such inmates
23 as it may have confined pursuant to the provisions of this compact.
24 ARTICLE IX
25 OTHER ARRANGEMENTS UNAFFECTED
26 Nothing contained in this compact shall be construed to abrogate or impair any agreement or other
27 arrangement which a party state may have with a nonparty state for the confinement, rehabilitation, or
28 treatment of inmates or to repeal any other laws of a party state authorizing the making of cooperative

- 2025

1 institutional arrangements.
2 ARTICLE X
3 CONSTRUCTION AND SEVERABILITY
4 The provisions of this compact shall be liberally construed and shall be severable. If any phrase,
5 clause, sentence, or provision of this compact is declared to be contrary to the constitution of any participating
6 state or of the United States or the applicability thereof to any government, agency, person, or circumstance is
7 held invalid, the validity of the remainder of this compact and the applicability thereof to any government,
8 agency, person, or circumstance shall not be affected thereby. If this compact shall be held contrary to the
9 constitution of any state participating therein, the compact shall remain in full force and effect as to the
10 remaining states and in full force and effect as to the state affected as to all severable matters."

18 Section 44. Section 49-1-102, MCA, is amended to read:
19 "49-1-102. Freedom from discrimination. (1) The right to be free from discrimination because of
20 race, creed, religion, color, sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], physical or mental disability, age, or national
21 origin is recognized as and declared to be a civil right. This right must include but not be limited to:
22 (a) the right to obtain and hold employment without discrimination; and
23 (b) the right to the full enjoyment of any of the accommodation facilities or privileges of any place
24 of public resort, accommodation, assemblage, or amusement.
25 (2) This section does not prevent the nonarbitrary consideration in adoption proceedings of
26 relevant information concerning the factors listed in subsection (1). Consideration of religious factors by a
27 licensed child-placing agency that is affiliated with a particular religious faith is not arbitrary consideration of
28 religion within the meaning of this section."

9 Section 48. Section 50-5-105, MCA, is amended to read:
10 "50-5-105. Discrimination prohibited. (1) All phases of the operation of a health care facility must be
11 without discrimination against anyone on the basis of race, creed, religion, color, national origin, sex, as defined
12 in 1-1-201 [section 1], age, marital status, physical or mental disability, or political ideas.
13 (2) (a) A health care facility may not refuse to admit a person to the facility solely because the
14 person has an HIV-related condition.
15 (b) For the purposes of this subsection (2), the following definitions apply:
16 (i) "HIV" means the human immunodeficiency virus identified as the causative agent of acquired
17 immunodeficiency syndrome (AIDS) and includes all HIV and HIV-related viruses that damage the cellular
18 branch of the human immune or neurological system and leave the infected person immunodeficient or
19 neurologically impaired.
20 (ii) "HIV-related condition" means any medical condition resulting from an HIV infection, including
21 but not limited to seropositivity for HIV.
22 (3) A person who operates a facility may not discriminate among the patients of licensed
23 physicians. The free and confidential professional relationship between a licensed physician and patient must
24 continue and remain unaffected.
25 (4) Except for a hospital that employs its medical staff, a hospital considering an application for
26 staff membership or granting privileges within the scope of the applicant's license may not deny the application
27 or privileges because the applicant is licensed under Title 37, chapter 6."
28

1 "50-19-103. Prenatal blood sample required for serological test. (1) Every female, as defined in 1-
2 1-201 [section 1], regardless of age or marital status, seeking prenatal care from a health care provider is
3 required to submit a blood specimen for the purpose of a standard serological test. In submitting the specimen
4 to the laboratory, the health care provider shall designate it as a prenatal test.
5 (2) A health care provider who attends a pregnant woman shall at the first professional visit take
6 the blood sample and submit it to a laboratory.
7 (3) A person permitted to attend a pregnant woman, but not permitted to take blood samples, must
8 have the sample taken by a person permitted to take blood samples and submit it to a laboratory.
9 (4) A health care provider who violates this part is guilty of a misdemeanor. However, a health care
10 provider who requests a sample of blood in accordance with this provision and whose request is refused is not
11 guilty of a violation of this section."

13 SECTION 53. SECTION 50-19-501, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:
14 "50-19-501. Nursing mother and infant protection. (1) The Montana legislature finds that
15 breastfeeding a baby is an important and basic act of nurturing that must be protected in the interests of
16 maternal and child health and family values. A mother, as defined in [section 1], has a right to breastfeed the
17 mother's child in any location, public or private, where the mother and child are otherwise authorized to be
18 present, irrespective of whether or not the mother's breast is covered during or incidental to the breastfeeding.
19 (2) A unit of local government may not prohibit breastfeeding in public by local ordinance.
20 (3) The act of breastfeeding may not be considered:
21 (a) a nuisance as provided in Title 27, chapter 30;
22 (b) indecent exposure as provided for in 45-5-504;
23 (c) sexual conduct as defined in 45-5-625; or
24 (d) obscenity as provided for in 45-8-201."

15 Section 57. Section 53-21-142, MCA, is amended to read:
16 "53-21-142. Rights of persons admitted to facility. Patients admitted to a mental health facility,
17 whether voluntarily or involuntarily, have the following rights:
18 (1) Patients have a right to privacy and dignity.
19 (2) Patients have a right to the least restrictive conditions necessary to achieve the purposes of
20 commitment. Patients must be accorded the right to appropriate treatment and related services in a setting and
21 under conditions that:
22 (a) are the most supportive of the patient's personal liberty; and
23 (b) restrict the patient's liberty only to the extent necessary and consistent with the patient's
24 treatment need, applicable requirements of law, and judicial orders.
25 (3) Patients have rights to visitation and reasonable access to telephone communications,
26 including the right to converse with others privately, except to the extent that the professional person
27 responsible for formulation of a particular patient's treatment plan writes an order imposing special restrictions.
28 The written order must be renewed after each periodic review of the treatment plan if any restrictions are to be

1 continued. Patients have an unrestricted right to visitation with attorneys, with spiritual counselors, and with

3 (4) Patients have an unrestricted right to send sealed mail. Patients have an unrestricted right to
4 receive sealed mail from their attorneys, private physicians and other professional persons, the mental
5 disabilities board of visitors, courts, and government officials. Patients have a right to receive sealed mail from
6 others except to the extent that a professional person responsible for formulation of a particular patient's

8 renewed after each periodic review of the treatment plan if any restrictions are to be continued.
9 (5) Patients have an unrestricted right to have access to letter-writing materials, including postage,
10 and have a right to have staff members of the facility assist persons who are unable to write, prepare, and mail
11 correspondence.
12 (6) Patients have a right to wear their own clothes and to keep and use their own personal
13 possessions, including toilet articles, except to the extent that clothes or personal possessions may be
14 determined by a professional person in charge of the patient's treatment plan to be dangerous or otherwise
15 inappropriate to the treatment regimen. The facility has an obligation to supply an adequate allowance of
16 clothing to any patients who do not have suitable clothing of their own. Patients must have the opportunity to
17 select from various types of neat, clean, and seasonable clothing. The clothing must be considered the patient's
18 throughout the patient's stay at the facility. The facility shall make provision for the laundering of patient
19 clothing.
20 (7) Patients have the right to keep and be allowed to spend a reasonable sum of their own money.
21 (8) Patients have the right to religious worship. Provisions for worship must be made available to
22 all patients on a nondiscriminatory basis. An individual may not be required to engage in any religious activities.
23 (9) Patients have a right to regular physical exercise several times a week. The facility shall
24 provide facilities and equipment for physical exercise. Patients have a right to be outdoors at regular and
25 frequent intervals in the absence of contrary medical considerations.

4 based facilities are appropriate and available and shall coordinate the patient's treatment for mental illness with

15 (a) regular housekeeping and maintenance procedures that will ensure that the facility is
16 maintained in a safe, clean, and attractive condition must be developed and implemented;
17 (b) there must be special provision made for geriatric and other nonambulatory patients to ensure
18 their safety and comfort, including special fittings on toilets and wheelchairs. Appropriate provision must be
19 made to permit nonambulatory patients to communicate their needs to the facility staff.
20 (c) pursuant to an established routine maintenance and repair program, the physical plant of each
21 facility must be kept in a continuous state of good repair and operation in accordance with the needs of the
22 health, comfort, safety, and well-being of the patients;
23 (d) each facility must meet all fire and safety standards established by the state and locality. In
24 addition, any hospital must meet the provisions of the life safety code of the national fire protection association
25 that are applicable to hospitals. A hospital must meet all standards established by the state for general
26 hospitals to the extent that they are relevant to psychiatric facilities.

28 (a) to be informed of the rights described in this section at the time of admission and periodically

16 exercising, and protecting the person's rights as described in this section.
17 (17) This section may not:
18 (a) obligate a professional person to administer treatment contrary to the professional's clinical
19 judgment;
20 (b) prevent a facility from discharging a patient for whom appropriate treatment, consistent with the
21 clinical judgment of a professional person responsible for the patient's treatment, is or has become impossible
22 to administer because of the patient's refusal to consent to the treatment;
23 (c) require a facility to admit a person who has, on prior occasions, repeatedly withheld consent to
24 appropriate treatment; or
25 (d) obligate a facility to treat a person admitted to the facility solely for diagnostic evaluation."

11 SECTION 59. SECTION 53-30-312, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:
12 "53-30-312. Creation of community corrections boards -- membership -- appointment -- terms --
13 compensation. (1) A unit of local government, the governing bodies of two or more units of local government,
14 or a tribal government may establish a community corrections board.
15 (2) A community corrections board consists of three to seven members, must, when possible, be
16 gender-balanced, as provided in [section 1], and have racial parity, and must include:
17 (a) one local law enforcement officer;
18 (b) one probation and parole officer; and
19 (c) one member of the public.
20 (3) Members of a community corrections board must be appointed by the chief executive officer of
21 the unit of local government or the tribal government in the judicial district in which community corrections
22 facilities or programs are established.
23 (4) Members of a community corrections board shall serve for a term of 4 years.
24 (5) Members of a community corrections board shall serve without compensation except as
25 otherwise decided by the units of local government or a tribal government."

15 (33) "Organization" means a corporation, business trust, estate, trust, partnership, joint venture,
16 association, government or governmental subdivision or agency, or any other legal or commercial entity.
17 (34) "Parent" includes any person entitled to take, or who would be entitled to take if the child died
18 without a will, as a parent under chapters 1 through 5 by intestate succession from the child whose relationship
19 is in question and excludes any person who is only a stepparent, foster parent, or grandparent.
20 (35) "Payor" means a trustee, insurer, business entity, employer, government, governmental agency
21 or subdivision, or any other person authorized or obligated by law or a governing instrument to make payments.
22 (36) "Person" means an individual, a corporation, an organization, or other legal entity.
23 (37) "Personal representative" includes executor, administrator, successor personal representative,
24 special administrator, and persons who perform substantially the same function under the law governing their
25 status. "General personal representative" excludes special administrator.
26 (38) "Petition" means a written request to the court for an order after notice.
27 (39) "Proceeding" includes action at law and suit in equity.
28 (40) "Property" includes both real and personal property or any interest in that property and means
- 92 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 anything that may be the subject of ownership.
2 (41) "Protected person" has the meaning provided in 72-5-101.
3 (42) "Protective proceeding" has the meaning provided in 72-5-101.
4 (43) "Record" means information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or that is stored in an
5 electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.
6 (44) "Security" includes any note; stock; treasury stock; bond; debenture; evidence of indebtedness;
7 certificate of interest or participation in an oil, gas, or mining title or lease or in payments out of production
8 under such a title or lease; collateral trust certificate; transferable share; voting trust certificate; in general, any
9 interest or instrument commonly known as a security; any certificate of interest or participation; or any
10 temporary or interim certificate, receipt, or certificate of deposit for or any warrant or right to subscribe to or
11 purchase any of the foregoing.
12 (45) "Settlement", in reference to a decedent's estate, includes the full process of administration,
13 distribution, and closing.
14 (46) "Sign" means, with present intent to authenticate or adopt a record other than a will:
15 (a) to execute or adopt a tangible symbol; or
16 (b) to attach to or logically associate with the record an electronic symbol, sound, or process.
17 (47) "Special administrator" means a personal representative as described by chapter 3, part 7.
18 (48) "State" means a state of the United States, the District of Columbia, the Commonwealth of
19 Puerto Rico, or any territory or insular possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.
20 (49) "Successor personal representative" means a personal representative, other than a special
21 administrator, who is appointed to succeed a previously appointed personal representative.
22 (50) "Successors" means persons, other than creditors, who are entitled to property of a decedent
23 under the decedent's will or chapters 1 through 5.
24 (51) "Supervised administration" refers to the proceedings described in chapter 3, part 4.
25 (52) "Survive" means that an individual has neither predeceased an event, including the death of
26 another individual, nor is considered to have predeceased an event under 72-2-114 or 72-2-712. The term
27 includes its derivatives, such as "survives", "survived", "survivor", and "surviving".
28 (53) "Testacy proceeding" means a proceeding to establish a will or determine intestacy.

1 (54) "Testator" includes an individual of either sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1].
2 (55) "Trust" includes an express trust, private or charitable, with additions to the trust, wherever and
3 however created. The term also includes a trust created or determined by judgment or decree under which the

19 SECTION 64. SECTION 72-17-106, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:
20 "72-17-106. Statewide organ and tissue donation registry. (1) The department of justice shall
21 electronically transfer to the federally designated organ procurement organization all information that appears
22 on the front of a driver's license, including the name, gender, as provided in [section 1], date of birth, and most
23 recent address of any person who obtains a driver's license and who volunteers to donate organs or tissue
24 upon death, as provided in 61-5-301. The department of justice may charge actual costs for the first transfer of
25 information, as provided in subsection (5). However, all subsequent electronic transfers of donor information
26 must be at no charge to the federally designated organ procurement organization.
27 (2) Information obtained by the federally designated organ procurement organization must be used
28 for the purpose of establishing a statewide organ and tissue donation registry accessible to in-state, recognized
- 94 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437
Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 cadaveric organ and cadaveric tissue agencies for the recovery or placement of organs and tissue and to
2 procurement agencies in another state when a Montana resident is a donor of an anatomical gift and is not
3 located in the state at the time of death or immediately before the death of the donor.
4 (3) An organ or tissue donation organization may not obtain information from the organ and tissue
5 donation registry for the purpose of fundraising. Organ and tissue donation registry information may not be
6 further disseminated unless authorized in this section or by federal law. Dissemination of organ and tissue
7 donation registry information may be made by the organ procurement organization to a recognized, in-state
8 procurement agency for other tissue recovery or to an out-of-state, federally designated organ procurement
9 organization.
10 (4) The federally designated organ procurement organization may acquire donor information from
11 sources other than the department of justice.
12 (5) All reasonable costs associated with the creation and maintenance of the organ and tissue
13 donation registry, as determined by the department of justice, must be paid by the organ and tissue
14 procurement organizations. Any money collected by the department of justice must be deposited in an account
15 in the state special revenue fund established by the department of justice for the purpose of the payment of
16 reasonable costs associated with the development and maintenance of the organ and tissue donation registry
17 and necessary for the initial installation and setup for electronic transfer of the donor information.
18 (6) An individual does not need to participate in the organ and tissue donation registry to be a
19 donor of organs or tissue. The registry is intended to facilitate organ and tissue donation and not inhibit persons
20 from being donors upon death."

26 agencies in the following functional areas:

15 NEW SECTION. Section 66. Repealer. The following section of the Montana Code Annotated is
16 repealed:
17 1-1-201. Terms of wide applicability.
18
19 NEW SECTION. Section 67. Codification instruction. [Section 1] is intended to be codified as an
20 integral part of Title 1, chapter 1, part 2, and the provisions of Title 1, chapter 1, part 2, apply to [section 1].
21
22 NEW SECTION. Section 68. Severability. If a part of [this act] is invalid, all valid parts that are
23 severable from the invalid part remain in effect. If a part of [this act] is invalid in one or more of its applications,
24 the part remains in effect in all valid applications that are severable from the invalid applications.
25
26 NEW SECTION. Section 69. Effective date. [This act] is effective on passage and approval.

Raw Text:
Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 SENATE BILL NO. 437
2 INTRODUCED BY C. GLIMM
3
4 A BILL FOR AN ACT ENTITLED: “AN ACT FOR THE CODIFICATION AND GENERAL REVISION OF THE
5 LAWS RELATING TO THE DEFINITION FOR THE WORDS SEX, FEMALE, AND MALE, MAN, WOMAN,
6 FATHER, AND MOTHER WHEN REFERRING TO A HUMAN; PROVIDING THAT THE DEFINITION OF SEX
7 REFERS TO BIOLOGICAL SEX AND NOT GENDER IDENTITY OR SEXUAL INTERCOURSE; PROVIDING
8 THAT THE DEFINITION OF SEX IS LIMITED TO TWO TYPES OF SEXES WHICH ARE REFERRED TO AS
9 MALE AND FEMALE; PROVIDING THAT THE DEFINITIONS OF MALE, AND FEMALE, MAN, WOMAN,
10 FATHER, AND MOTHER REFER TO BIOLOGICAL SEX AND NOT SUBJECTIVE GENDER IDENTITY;
11 CLARIFYING THE MEANING OF THE TERM "GENDER"; PROVIDING FOR EXCEPTIONS; AMENDING
12 SECTIONS 2-18-208, 2-18-606, 7-15-4207, 7-34-2123, 10-2-403, 13-27-408, 13-35-301, 13-38-201, 13-38-
13 203, 13-38-205, 19-2-802, 20-6-808, 20-7-1306, 20-7-1703, 20-9-327, 20-11-116, 20-25-501, 20-25-707, 22-2-
14 306, 23-2-505, 33-1-201, 35-20-209, 39-2-912, 39-29-101, 39-71-401, 40-1-107, 40-1-311, 40-1-401, 40-5-804,
15 40-5-907, 40-5-1031, 40-6-701, 40-6-703, 41-3-210, 41-5-103, 42-2-204, 44-2-411, 44-2-412, 45-5-625, 46-18-
16 101, 46-19-301, 46-19-401, 49-1-102, 49-2-101, 49-3-101, 50-4-720, 50-5-105, 50-5-602, 50-11-101, 50-15-
17 101, 50-19-103, 50-19-501, 50-60-214, 53-20-142, 53-21-121, 53-21-142, 53-24-310, 53-30-312, 60-5-514, 60-
18 5-522, 61-5-107, 72-1-103, 72-17-106, AND 90-14-104, MCA; REPEALING SECTION 1-1-201, MCA; AND
19 PROVIDING AN IMMEDIATE EFFECTIVE DATE.”
20
21 WHEREAS, IN HUMAN BEINGS, THERE ARE TWO -- AND ONLY TWO -- SEXES: MALE AND FEMALE, WHICH REFER
22 TO THE TWO BODY STRUCTURES (PHENOTYPES) THAT, IN NORMAL DEVELOPMENT, CORRESPOND TO ONE OR THE OTHER
23 GAMETE -- SPERM FOR MALES AND OVA FOR FEMALES; AND
24 WHEREAS, EVERY INDIVIDUAL IS EITHER MALE OR FEMALE; AND
25 WHEREAS, AN INDIVIDUAL'S SEX CAN BE OBSERVED OR CLINICALLY VERIFIED AT OR BEFORE BIRTH; AND
26 WHEREAS, RARE DISORDERS OF SEXUAL DEVELOPMENT ARE NOT EXCEPTIONS TO THE BINARY NATURE OF
27 SEX; AND
28 WHEREAS, IN NO CASE IS AN INDIVIDUAL'S SEX DETERMINED BY STIPULATION OR SELF-IDENTIFICATION; AND
- 1 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 WHEREAS, THERE IS INCREASING CONFUSION ABOUT THE DEFINITION AND IMPLICATIONS OF SEX AS A
2 BIOLOGICAL TRUTH AND ITS RELATIONSHIP TO CONCEPTS AND TERMS INCLUDING BUT NOT LIMITED TO SEX ASSIGNED AT
3 BIRTH, GENDER, GENDER IDENTITY, GENDER ROLE, GENDER EXPRESSION, AND EXPERIENCED GENDER; AND
4 WHEREAS, CONFUSION AND AMBIGUITIES SURROUNDING THE DEFINITIONS OF SEX, MALE, FEMALE, AND
5 RELATED TERMS CAN HINDER INDIVIDUAL EFFORTS TO ENJOY EQUAL TREATMENT UNDER THE LAW; AND
6 WHEREAS, LEGAL EQUALITY OF THE TWO SEXES -- MALE AND FEMALE -- DOES NOT IMPLY THAT THE SEXES
7 ARE IDENTICAL TO EACH OTHER OR ARE THE SAME IN EVERY RESPECT; AND
8 WHEREAS, WITH RESPECT TO THE TWO SEXES -- MALE AND FEMALE -- SEPARATE FACILITIES OR SPORTS
9 LEAGUES ESTABLISHED BECAUSE OF OR ORGANIZED ACCORDING TO PHYSICAL DIFFERENCES BETWEEN THE SEXES DO
10 NOT CONSTITUTE UNEQUAL TREATMENT UNDER THE LAW; AND
11 WHEREAS, PHYSICAL DIFFERENCES BETWEEN MALES AND FEMALES ARE ENDURING, AND THE TWO SEXES ARE
12 NOT FUNGIBLE.
13 THEREFORE, IT IS THE INTENT OF THE LEGISLATURE OF THIS STATE TO CLARIFY AND RECONCILE THE
14 MEANING OF SEX, MALE, FEMALE, AND RELATED TERMS IN STATE LAWS, ADMINISTRATIVE RULES, AND GUIDELINES.
15
16 BE IT ENACTED BY THE LEGISLATURE OF THE STATE OF MONTANA:
17
18 NEW SECTION. Section 1. Terms of wide applicability. (1) Unless the context requires otherwise,
19 the following definitions apply in the Montana Code Annotated:
20 (a) "FATHER" MEANS A MALE PARENT.
21 (B) "Female" means a member of the human species who, under normal development, has XX
22 chromosomes and produces or would produce relatively large, relatively immobile gametes, or eggs, during her
23 life cycle and has a reproductive and endocrine system oriented around the production of those gametes. An
24 individual who would otherwise fall within this definition, but for a biological or genetic condition, is female, WHEN
25 USED TO REFER TO A NATURAL PERSON, AN INDIVIDUAL WHO NATURALLY HAS, HAD, WILL HAVE, OR WOULD HAVE, BUT
26 FOR A CONGENITAL ANOMALY OR INTENTIONAL OR UNINTENTIONAL DISRUPTION, THE REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEM THAT AT
27 SOME POINT PRODUCES, TRANSPORTS, AND UTILIZES THE LARGE GAMETE, OR OVA, FOR FERTILIZATION.
28 (b)(C) "Male" means a member of the human species who, under normal development, has XY
- 2 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 chromosomes and produces or would produce small, mobile gametes, or sperm, during his life cycle and has a
2 reproductive and endocrine system oriented around the production of those gametes. An individual who would
3 otherwise fall within this definition, but for a biological or genetic condition, is male, WHEN USED TO REFER TO A
4 NATURAL PERSON, AN INDIVIDUAL WHO NATURALLY HAS, HAD, WILL HAVE, OR WOULD HAVE, BUT FOR A CONGENITAL
5 ANOMALY OR INTENTIONAL OR UNINTENTIONAL DISRUPTION, THE REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEM THAT AT SOME POINT
6 PRODUCES, TRANSPORTS, AND UTILIZES THE SMALL GAMETE, OR SPERM, FOR FERTILIZATION.
7 (c)(D) "MAN" MEANS AN ADULT HUMAN MALE, EXCEPT WHEN USED AS A GENERIC REFERENCE TO HUMAN
8 BEINGS.
9 (E) "MOTHER" MEANS A FEMALE PARENT.
10 (F) "Oath" includes an affirmation or declaration.
11 (d)(G) "Person" includes a corporation or other entity as well as a natural person.
12 (e)(H) "Several" means two or more.
13 (f)(I) "Sex" means the organization of the body parts and gametes for reproduction in human beings
14 and other organisms. In human beings, there are exactly two sexes, male and female, with two corresponding
15 types of gametes. The sexes are determined by the biological and genetic indication of male or female,
16 including sex chromosomes, naturally occurring sex chromosomes, gonads, and nonambiguous internal and
17 external genitalia present at birth, without regard to an individual's psychological, behavioral, social, chosen, or
18 subjective experience of gender WHETHER SOMEONE IS MALE OR FEMALE, WHICH IS DISTINGUISHED BASED ON THE
19 TYPE OF GAMETE, SPERM OR EGGS, THEY ARE CAPABLE OF OR EXPECTED TO PRODUCE, AS DICTATED BY THEIR PRIMARY
20 SEXUAL ANATOMY. BECAUSE THERE ARE ONLY TWO TYPES OF GAMETES, SPERM AND OVA, WITH TWO CORRESPONDING
21 REPRODUCTIVE SYSTEMS, THERE ARE ONLY TWO SEXES: MALE AND FEMALE. AN INDIVIDUAL'S SEX IS ROOTED IN
22 REPRODUCTIVE ANATOMY AND IS IN NO WAY INFLUENCED OR DEFINED BY ONE'S PSYCHOLOGICAL STATE, BEHAVIOR,
23 EXPRESSION, OR PERSONAL IDENTITY.
24 (g)(J) "State", when applied to the different parts of the United States, includes the District of
25 Columbia and the territories.
26 (h)(K) "United States" includes the District of Columbia and the territories.
27 (L) "WOMAN" MEANS AN ADULT HUMAN FEMALE.
28 (2) Wherever the word "man" or "men" or a word that includes the syllable "man" or "men" in
- 3 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 combination with other syllables, such as "workman", appears in this code, the word or syllable includes
2 "woman" or "women" unless the context clearly indicates a contrary intent and unless the subject matter of the
3 statute relates clearly and necessarily to a specific sex only.
4 (3) Whenever the term "heretofore" occurs in any statute, it must be construed to mean any time
5 previous to the day the statute takes effect. Whenever the word "hereafter" occurs, it must be construed to
6 mean the time after the statute containing the term takes effect.
7 (4) (A) THE TERM "GENDER", WHEN USED ALONE TO REFER TO A MALE, FEMALE, OR THE NATURAL
8 DIFFERENCES BETWEEN A MALE AND FEMALE:
9 (I) MUST BE CONSIDERED A SYNONYM FOR SEX; AND
10 (II) MAY NOT BE CONSIDERED A SYNONYM OR SHORT-HAND EXPRESSION FOR GENDER IDENTITY,
11 EXPERIENCED GENDER, GENDER EXPRESSION, OR GENDER ROLE.
12 (B) THE TERM "GENDER" DOES NOT APPLY WHEN IT IS USED IN CONJUNCTION WITH OTHER WORDS OR AS
13 AN ADJECTIVE TO MODIFY OTHER WORDS, OR WHEN CONTEXT OR EXPLICIT DEFINITION IN PREEXISTING STATE LAW,
14 ADMINISTRATIVE RULES, OR GUIDELINES INDICATES OTHERWISE.
15 (C) THE TERM "GENDER IDENTITY", IF USED IN STATE LAW, ADMINISTRATIVE RULES, OR GUIDELINES, MAY
16 NOT BE CONSIDERED A SYNONYM OR SUBSTITUTE FOR SEX OR GENDER.

18 Section 2. Section 2-18-208, MCA, is amended to read:
19 "2-18-208. Comparable worth. The department of administration shall, in its continuous efforts to
20 enhance the current classification plan and pay schedules, work toward the goal of establishing a standard of
21 equal pay for comparable worth. This standard for the classification plan shall be reached by:
22 (1) eliminating, in the classification of positions, the use of judgments and factors that contain
23 inherent biases based on sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1]; and
24 (2) comparing, in the classification of positions, the factors for determining job worth across
25 occupational groups whenever those groups are dominated by males or females."

17 Section 8. Section 13-35-301, MCA, is amended to read:
18 "13-35-301. Adoption of code of fair campaign practices. The following code of fair campaign
19 practices is adopted by Montana:
20 "There are basic principles of decency, honesty, and fair play that every candidate for public office in
21 the United States has a moral obligation to observe and uphold, in order that, after vigorously contested but
22 fairly conducted campaigns, our citizens may exercise their constitutional right to a free and untrammeled
23 choice and the will of the people may be fully and clearly expressed on the issues before the country.
24 Therefore:
25 I will conduct my campaign in the best American tradition, discussing the issues as I see them,
26 presenting my record and policies with sincerity and frankness, and criticizing without fear or favor the record
27 and policies of my opponent and my opponent's party that merit such criticism.
28 I will defend and uphold the right of every qualified American voter to full and equal participation in the

Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 electoral process.
2 I will conduct my campaign without the use of personal vilification, character defamation, whispering
3 campaigns, libel, slander, or scurrilous attacks on my opposition or my opposition's personal or family life.
4 I will not use campaign material of any sort that misrepresents, distorts, or otherwise falsifies the facts,
5 nor will I use malicious or unfounded accusations that aim at creating or exploiting doubts, without justification,
6 as to the loyalty and patriotism of my opposition.
7 I will not make any appeal to prejudice based on race, sex, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], creed, or
8 national origin.
9 I will not undertake or condone any dishonest or unethical practice that tends to corrupt or undermine
10 our American system of free elections or that hampers or prevents the full and free expression of the will of the
11 voters.
12 Insofar as is possible, I will immediately and publicly repudiate support deriving from any individual or
13 group that resorts, on behalf of my candidacy or in opposition to that of my opponent, to the methods and
14 tactics that I have pledged not to use or condone.""

3 SECTION 11. SECTION 13-38-205, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:
4 "13-38-205. Organization and operation of county and city central committees. (1) The county
5 central committee shall meet prior to the state convention of its political party and organize by electing a
6 presiding officer and one or more vice presiding officers. The gender, as provided in [section 1], of the presiding
7 officer and the vice presiding officer may not be the same. The county central committee shall elect a secretary
8 and other officers as necessary. It is not necessary for the officers to be precinct committee representatives.
9 (2) The committee may select managing or executive committees and authorize subcommittees to
10 exercise all powers conferred upon the county, city, state, and congressional central committees by the election
11 laws of this state.
12 (3) The presiding officer of the county central committee shall call the county convention and not
13 less than 4 days before the date of the county convention shall publish the call in a newspaper published at the
14 county seat and mail a copy of the call to each precinct committee representative. If party rules permit the use
15 of a proxy, a proxy may not be recognized unless it is held by an elector of the precinct of the committee
16 representative executing it.
17 (4) The county presiding officer of the party shall preside at the county convention. No person
18 other than a duly elected or appointed committee representative or officer of the committee is entitled to
19 participate in the proceedings of the committee.
20 (5) If a committee representative is absent, the convention may fill the vacancy by appointing some
21 qualified elector of the party, resident in the precinct, to represent the precinct in the convention.
22 (6) The county convention shall elect delegates and alternate delegates to the state convention
23 under rules of the state party. The presiding officer and secretary of the county convention shall issue and sign
24 certificates of election of the delegates."

12 SECTION 21. SECTION 23-2-505, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:
13 "23-2-505. Owner's civil liability. The owner of a vessel is liable for any injury or damage
14 occasioned by the negligent operation of the vessel, whether the negligence consists of a violation of the
15 provisions of the statutes of this state or neglecting to observe ordinary care and operation that the rules of the
16 common law require. However, the owner is not liable unless the vessel is being used with the owner's express
17 or implied consent. It must be presumed that the vessel is being operated with the knowledge and consent of
18 the owner if, at the time of the injury or damage, it is under the control of the owner's spouse, father as defined
19 in [section 1], mother as defined in [section 1], brother, sister, son, daughter, or other immediate member of the
20 owner's family. This section may not be construed to relieve any other person from any liability that the person
21 would otherwise have. However, this section may not be construed to authorize or permit any recovery in
22 excess of injury or damage actually incurred."

18 the relationship is by the half or the whole blood, or between first cousins;

22 (2) Parties to a marriage prohibited under this section who cohabit after removal of the impediment
23 are lawfully married as of the date of the removal of the impediment.
24 (3) Children born of a prohibited marriage are legitimate.
25 (4) A contractual relationship entered into for the purpose of achieving a civil relationship that is
26 prohibited under subsection (1) is void as against public policy."

14 Section 33. Section 40-6-701, MCA, is amended to read:
15 "40-6-701. Interference with fundamental parental rights restricted -- cause of action. (1) A
16 government entity may not interfere with the fundamental right of parents to direct the upbringing, education,
17 health care, and mental health of their children unless the government entity demonstrates that the
18 interference:
19 (a) furthers a compelling governmental interest; and
20 (b) is narrowly tailored and is the least restrictive means available for the furthering of the
21 compelling governmental interest.

23 obstruction or interference by a government entity, including but not limited to the rights and responsibilities to
24 do the following:
25 (a) direct the education of the child, including the right to choose public, private, religious, or home

18 "45-5-625. Sexual abuse of children. (1) A person commits the offense of sexual abuse of children if

20 (a) knowingly employs, uses, or permits the employment or use of a child in an exhibition of sexual
