14 SECTION 41. SECTION 46-18-101, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:
15 "46-18-101. Correctional and sentencing policy. (1) It is the purpose of this section to establish the
16 correctional and sentencing policy of the state of Montana. Laws for the punishment of crime are drawn to
17 implement the policy established by this section.
18 (2) The correctional and sentencing policy of the state of Montana is to:
19 (a) punish each offender commensurate with the nature and degree of harm caused by the offense
20 and to hold an offender accountable;
21 (b) protect the public, reduce crime, and increase the public sense of safety by incarcerating
22 violent offenders and serious repeat offenders;
23 (c) provide restitution, reparation, and restoration to the victim of the offense; and
24 (d) encourage and provide opportunities for the offender's self-improvement to provide
25 rehabilitation and reintegration of offenders back into the community.
26 (3) To achieve the policy outlined in subsection (2), the state of Montana adopts the following
27 principles:
28 (a) Sentencing and punishment must be certain, timely, consistent, and understandable.
- 53 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 (b) Sentences should be commensurate with the punishment imposed on other persons
2 committing the same offenses.
3 (c) Sentencing practices must be neutral with respect to the offender's race, gender, as provided in
4 [section 1], religion, national origin, or social or economic status.
5 (d) Sentencing practices must permit judicial discretion to consider aggravating and mitigating
6 circumstances.
7 (e) Sentencing practices must include punishing violent and serious repeat felony offenders with
8 incarceration.
9 (f) Sentencing practices must provide alternatives to imprisonment for the punishment of those
10 nonviolent felony offenders who do not have serious criminal records.
11 (g) Sentencing and correctional practices must emphasize that the offender is responsible for
12 obeying the law and must hold the offender accountable for the offender's actions.
13 (h) Sentencing practices must emphasize restitution to the victim by the offender. A sentence must
14 require an offender who is financially able to do so to pay restitution, costs as provided in 46-18-232, costs of
15 assigned counsel, as provided in 46-8-113, and, if the offender is a sex offender, costs of any chemical
16 treatment.
17 (i) Sentencing practices should promote and support practices, policies, and programs that focus
18 on restorative justice principles."

24 WESTERN INTERSTATE CORRECTIONS COMPACT
25 ARTICLE I
26 PURPOSE AND POLICY
27 The party states, desiring by common action to improve their institutional facilities and provide
28 programs of sufficiently high quality for the confinement, treatment, and rehabilitation of various types of
- 54 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary

1 offenders, declare that it is the policy of each of the party states to provide such facilities and programs on the
2 basis of cooperation with one another, thereby serving the best interests of such offenders and of society. The
3 purpose of this compact is to provide for the development and execution of such programs of cooperation for
4 the confinement, treatment, and rehabilitation of offenders.
5 ARTICLE II
6 DEFINITIONS
7 As used in this compact, unless the context clearly requires otherwise:
8 (1) "state" means a state of the United States or, subject to the limitation contained in Article VII,
9 Guam;
10 (2) "sending state" means a state party to this compact in which conviction was had;
11 (3) "receiving state" means a state party to this compact to which an inmate is sent for confinement
12 other than a state in which conviction was had;
13 (4) "inmate" means a male or female, as defined in 1-1-201 [section 1], offender who is under
14 sentence to or confined in a prison or other correctional institution;
15 (5) "institution" means any prison, reformatory, or other correctional facility (including but not
16 limited to a facility for the mentally ill or mentally defective) in which inmates may lawfully be confined.
17 ARTICLE III
18 CONTRACTS
19 (1) Each party state may make one or more contracts with any one or more of the other party
20 states for the confinement of inmates on behalf of a sending state in institutions situated within receiving states.
21 Any such contract shall provide for:
22 (a) its duration;
23 (b) payments to be made to the receiving state by the sending state for inmate maintenance,
24 extraordinary medical and dental expenses, and any participation in or receipt by inmates of rehabilitative or
25 correctional services, facilities, programs, or treatment not reasonably included as part of normal maintenance;
26 (c) participation in programs of inmate employment, if any; the disposition or crediting of any

13 within such state a criminal offense, the inmate shall not be returned without the consent of the receiving state
14 until discharged from prosecution or other form of proceeding, imprisonment, or detention for such offense. The

18 compact shall be deemed a fugitive from the sending state and from the state in which the institution is situated.

20 institution of extradition proceedings shall be that of the sending state, but nothing contained herein shall be
21 construed to prevent or affect the activities of officers and agencies of any jurisdiction directed toward the
22 apprehension and return of an escapee.

3 ARTICLE VII
4 ENTRY INTO FORCE
5 This compact shall enter into force and become effective and binding upon the states so acting when it
6 has been enacted into law by any two contiguous states from among the states of Alaska, Arizona, California,
7 Colorado, Hawaii, Idaho, Montana, Nebraska, Nevada, New Mexico, Oregon, Utah, Washington, and Wyoming.
8 For the purposes of this article, Alaska and Hawaii shall be deemed contiguous to each other; to any and all of
9 the states of California, Oregon, and Washington; and to Guam. Thereafter, this compact shall enter into force
10 and become effective and binding as to any other of said states or any other state contiguous to at least one
11 party state upon similar action by such state. Guam may become party to this compact by taking action similar
12 to that provided for joinder by any other eligible party state and upon the consent of congress to such joinder.
13 For the purposes of this article, Guam shall be deemed contiguous to Alaska, Hawaii, California, Oregon, and
14 Washington.
15 ARTICLE VIII
16 WITHDRAWAL AND TERMINATION
17 This compact shall continue in force and remain binding upon a party state until it shall have enacted a
18 statute repealing the same and providing for the sending of formal written notice of withdrawal from the
19 compact to the appropriate officials of all other party states. An actual withdrawal shall not take effect until 2
20 years after the notices provided in said statute have been sent. Such withdrawal shall not relieve the
21 withdrawing state from its obligations assumed hereunder prior to the effective date of withdrawal. Before the
22 effective date of withdrawal, a withdrawing state shall remove to its territory, at its own expense, such inmates
23 as it may have confined pursuant to the provisions of this compact.
24 ARTICLE IX
25 OTHER ARRANGEMENTS UNAFFECTED
26 Nothing contained in this compact shall be construed to abrogate or impair any agreement or other
27 arrangement which a party state may have with a nonparty state for the confinement, rehabilitation, or
28 treatment of inmates or to repeal any other laws of a party state authorizing the making of cooperative

- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 institutional arrangements.
2 ARTICLE X
3 CONSTRUCTION AND SEVERABILITY
4 The provisions of this compact shall be liberally construed and shall be severable. If any phrase,
5 clause, sentence, or provision of this compact is declared to be contrary to the constitution of any participating
6 state or of the United States or the applicability thereof to any government, agency, person, or circumstance is
7 held invalid, the validity of the remainder of this compact and the applicability thereof to any government,
8 agency, person, or circumstance shall not be affected thereby. If this compact shall be held contrary to the
9 constitution of any state participating therein, the compact shall remain in full force and effect as to the
10 remaining states and in full force and effect as to the state affected as to all severable matters."

17 PURPOSE AND POLICY
18 The party states, desiring by common action to fully utilize and improve their institutional facilities and
19 provide adequate programs for the confinement, treatment and rehabilitation of various types of offenders,
20 declare that it is the policy of each of the party states to provide such facilities and programs on a basis of
21 cooperation with one another, thereby serving the best interests of such offenders and of society and effecting
22 economies in capital expenditures and operational costs. The purpose of this compact is to provide for the
23 mutual development and execution of such programs of cooperation for the confinement, treatment and
24 rehabilitation of offenders with the most economical use of human and material resources.

3 compact shall be deemed a fugitive from the sending state and from the state in which the institution is situated.
4 In the case of an escape to a jurisdiction other than the sending or receiving state, the responsibility for
5 institution of extradition or rendition proceedings shall be that of the sending state, but nothing contained herein
6 shall be construed to prevent or affect the activities of officers and agencies of any jurisdiction directed toward
7 the apprehension and return of an escapee.
8 ARTICLE VI
9 FEDERAL AID
10 Any state party to this compact may accept federal aid for use in connection with any institution or
11 program, the use of which is or may be affected by this compact or any contract pursuant hereto and any
12 inmate in a receiving state pursuant to this compact may participate in any such federally aided program or
13 activity for which the sending and receiving states have made contractual provision, provided that if such
14 program or activity is not part of the customary correctional regimen, the express consent of the appropriate
15 official of the sending state shall be required therefor.
16 ARTICLE VII
17 ENTRY INTO FORCE
18 This compact shall enter into force and become effective and binding upon the states so acting when it
19 has been enacted into law by any two states. Thereafter, this compact shall enter into force and become
20 effective and binding as to any other of said states upon similar action by such state.
21 ARTICLE VIII
22 WITHDRAWAL AND TERMINATION
23 This compact shall continue in force and remain binding upon a party state until it shall have enacted a
24 statute repealing the same and providing for the sending of formal written notice of withdrawal from the
25 compact to the appropriate officials of all other party states. An actual withdrawal shall not take effect until one
26 year after the notices provided in said statute have been sent. Such withdrawal shall not relieve the withdrawing
27 state from its obligations assumed hereunder prior to the effective date of withdrawal. Before the effective date
28 of withdrawal, a withdrawing state shall remove to its territory, at its own expense, such inmates as it may have
- 64 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 confined pursuant to the provisions of this compact.
2 ARTICLE IX
3 OTHER ARRANGEMENTS UNAFFECTED
4 Nothing contained in this compact shall be construed to abrogate or impair any agreement or other
5 arrangement which a party state may have with a nonparty state for the confinement, rehabilitation or treatment
6 of inmates nor to repeal any other laws of a party state authorizing the making of cooperative institutional
7 arrangements.
8 ARTICLE X
9 CONSTRUCTION AND SEVERABILITY
10 The provisions of this compact shall be liberally construed and shall be severable. If any phrase,
11 clause, sentence or provision of this compact is declared to be contrary to the constitution of any participating
12 state or of the United States or the applicability thereof to any government, agency, person or circumstance is
13 held invalid, the validity of the remainder of this compact and the applicability thereof to any government,
14 agency, person or circumstance shall not be affected thereby. If this compact shall be held contrary to the
15 constitution of any state participating therein, the compact shall remain in full force and effect as to the
16 remaining states and in full force and effect as to the state affected as to all severable matters."
17

11 SECTION 59. SECTION 53-30-312, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:
12 "53-30-312. Creation of community corrections boards -- membership -- appointment -- terms --
13 compensation. (1) A unit of local government, the governing bodies of two or more units of local government,
14 or a tribal government may establish a community corrections board.
15 (2) A community corrections board consists of three to seven members, must, when possible, be
16 gender-balanced, as provided in [section 1], and have racial parity, and must include:
17 (a) one local law enforcement officer;
18 (b) one probation and parole officer; and
19 (c) one member of the public.
20 (3) Members of a community corrections board must be appointed by the chief executive officer of
21 the unit of local government or the tribal government in the judicial district in which community corrections
22 facilities or programs are established.
23 (4) Members of a community corrections board shall serve for a term of 4 years.
24 (5) Members of a community corrections board shall serve without compensation except as
25 otherwise decided by the units of local government or a tribal government."

24 in the case of a devise to an existing trust or trustee or to a trustee or trust described by will, the trust or trustee
25 is the devisee and the beneficiaries are not devisees.
26 (13) "Disability" means cause for a protective order as described by 72-5-409.
27 (14) "Distributee" means any person who has received property of a decedent from the decedent's
28 personal representative other than as a creditor or purchaser. A testamentary trustee is a distributee only to the

18 pursuant to testamentary or court appointment but excludes one who is merely a guardian ad litem.

20 the state, who are entitled under the statutes of intestate succession to the property of a decedent.

19 SECTION 64. SECTION 72-17-106, MCA, IS AMENDED TO READ:
20 "72-17-106. Statewide organ and tissue donation registry. (1) The department of justice shall
21 electronically transfer to the federally designated organ procurement organization all information that appears
22 on the front of a driver's license, including the name, gender, as provided in [section 1], date of birth, and most
23 recent address of any person who obtains a driver's license and who volunteers to donate organs or tissue
24 upon death, as provided in 61-5-301. The department of justice may charge actual costs for the first transfer of
25 information, as provided in subsection (5). However, all subsequent electronic transfers of donor information
26 must be at no charge to the federally designated organ procurement organization.
27 (2) Information obtained by the federally designated organ procurement organization must be used
28 for the purpose of establishing a statewide organ and tissue donation registry accessible to in-state, recognized
- 94 - Authorized Print Version – SB 437

Amendment - 1st Reading/2nd House-blue - Requested by: Ed Stafman - (H) Judiciary
- 2025
69th Legislature 2025 Drafter: Rachel Weiss, SB0437.002.005
1 cadaveric organ and cadaveric tissue agencies for the recovery or placement of organs and tissue and to
2 procurement agencies in another state when a Montana resident is a donor of an anatomical gift and is not
3 located in the state at the time of death or immediately before the death of the donor.
4 (3) An organ or tissue donation organization may not obtain information from the organ and tissue
5 donation registry for the purpose of fundraising. Organ and tissue donation registry information may not be
6 further disseminated unless authorized in this section or by federal law. Dissemination of organ and tissue
7 donation registry information may be made by the organ procurement organization to a recognized, in-state
8 procurement agency for other tissue recovery or to an out-of-state, federally designated organ procurement
9 organization.
10 (4) The federally designated organ procurement organization may acquire donor information from
11 sources other than the department of justice.
12 (5) All reasonable costs associated with the creation and maintenance of the organ and tissue
13 donation registry, as determined by the department of justice, must be paid by the organ and tissue
14 procurement organizations. Any money collected by the department of justice must be deposited in an account
15 in the state special revenue fund established by the department of justice for the purpose of the payment of
16 reasonable costs associated with the development and maintenance of the organ and tissue donation registry
17 and necessary for the initial installation and setup for electronic transfer of the donor information.
18 (6) An individual does not need to participate in the organ and tissue donation registry to be a
19 donor of organs or tissue. The registry is intended to facilitate organ and tissue donation and not inhibit persons
20 from being donors upon death."

15 NEW SECTION. Section 66. Repealer. The following section of the Montana Code Annotated is
16 repealed:
17 1-1-201. Terms of wide applicability.

19 NEW SECTION. Section 67. Codification instruction. [Section 1] is intended to be codified as an
20 integral part of Title 1, chapter 1, part 2, and the provisions of Title 1, chapter 1, part 2, apply to [section 1].
21
22 NEW SECTION. Section 68. Severability. If a part of [this act] is invalid, all valid parts that are
23 severable from the invalid part remain in effect. If a part of [this act] is invalid in one or more of its applications,
24 the part remains in effect in all valid applications that are severable from the invalid applications.
25
26 NEW SECTION. Section 69. Effective date. [This act] is effective on passage and approval.
